    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b1e6ff39-b292-4e3f-be67-09cff93af596'

  <span id="freeText14939055416524409935" style="display:none">A Seductive Nighttime World. . . Dr. Emily Drake's psychotherapy patients tend to be a little unusual. Instead of midlife crises and mother fixations, Emily treats vampires with blood phobias and sex-demons looking for meaningful relationships. But healing these powerful beings requires an important rule: Never trust a shifter. Especially not one like Detective Colin Gyth, whose gold-flecked eyes and predatory air make Emily realize how much she longs to lose control. . .<br /><br />A Dark And Dangerous Hunger. . .<br /><br />Colin can't believe the doctor he has to work with on the Night Butcher murder case is the one person who could expose his true identity as a wolf shifter. Smart and sexy, Emily brings out the alpha male in Colin, unleashing a wild desire that takes them both over the edge. . . But in the shadows, the Night Butcher waits, eager to spill Emily's blood and taste her terror. And he'll use any means to destroy her, including the one person she has grown to trust. . .</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53252976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5953416181447579850"><br/>I read this book awhile back and don't have a lot of recollection of the details of the story however, I do recall having a hard time forming any real connection with the characters, but I did enjoy the plot. To be honest, my favorite parts of the book were the sessions with Dr. Emily Drake's psychotherapy patients. A Succubus who wanted to be looked at as more than just a sex symbol, a vampire who didn't want to drink blood... those were some funny characters!<br/><br/>While I think this book suffers fro</span>
  <span id="freeText5953416181447579850" style="display:none"><br />I read this book awhile back and don't have a lot of recollection of the details of the story however, I do recall having a hard time forming any real connection with the characters, but I did enjoy the plot. To be honest, my favorite parts of the book were the sessions with Dr. Emily Drake's psychotherapy patients. A Succubus who wanted to be looked at as more than just a sex symbol, a vampire who didn't want to drink blood... those were some funny characters!<br /><br />While I think this book suffers from FITSs, <i>First In The Series syndrome </i> it was still a good read and I plan to continue the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5953416181447579850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_118639638" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/118639638" />
    <a title="Quinn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2310262-quinn"><img alt="Quinn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300839213p2/2310262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/118639638?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Quinn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Quinn" href="/user/show/2310262-quinn">Quinn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780758226037" href="/book/show/6528937-hotter-after-midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2310262-quinn?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2310262-quinn?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2310262-quinn?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer118639638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10449359771216389842"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Author Jacquelyn Frank describes this book as “A cross between CSI and Medium, only hotter and with a hero that truly has bite!”, and that is a fairly apt summation. <i>Hotter After Midnight</i> is an unusual mix of police procedural, paranormal romance and suspense. <br/><br/>Dr. Emily Drake is a psychotherapist who specialises in treating <i>Other</i> - supernatural beings whose existence is still considered myth and fairytale by most of humankind. Her psychic gift of awareness and the ability to see into mi</span>
  <span id="freeText10449359771216389842" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />Author Jacquelyn Frank describes this book as “A cross between CSI and Medium, only hotter and with a hero that truly has bite!”, and that is a fairly apt summation. <i>Hotter After Midnight</i> is an unusual mix of police procedural, paranormal romance and suspense. <br /><br />Dr. Emily Drake is a psychotherapist who specialises in treating <i>Other</i> - supernatural beings whose existence is still considered myth and fairytale by most of humankind. Her psychic gift of awareness and the ability to see into minds only works with <i>Other</i>, and so she treats vampires with blood phobias and succubus seeking relationships based on something other than sex.<br /><br />Detective Colin Gyth is a shifter – not that his colleagues on the force know this. Most of them aren’t even aware that such a thing exists, and experience has told him that it’s best to keep things that way. But when Emily is called in as profiler on the Night Butcher case, Colin knows that she is the one person who could expose his true identity.<br /><br />While investigating the case, Emily and Colin find themselves caught up in the secret Demon underworld as they try to keep Colin’s secret and catch a supernatural serial killer before he strikes again, makes them his next victim, or betrays the existence of <i>Others</i> to the world.<br /><br />Although not my preferred approach, there are times where the insta-lust trope works just fine for me. Unfortunately, this book was not one of them. It came out of nowhere with minimal explanation, before we had a chance to really get to know either of the characters, and then permeated the entire book.<br /><br />I did enjoy <i>Hotter After Midnight</i>, particularly the middle section, but it would have been significantly improved by developing the characters rather than just moving the suspense plot forward. The explanation of the serial killer’s motive was also extremely anti-climatic and disappointing.<br /><br />This is the first book in the midnight trilogy, and I liked the world the author created enough to continue with the next books – <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3294489.Midnight_Sins__Midnight___2_" title="Midnight Sins (Midnight, #2) by Cynthia Eden" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight Sins</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6177429.Midnight_s_Master__Midnight___3_" title="Midnight's Master (Midnight, #3) by Cynthia Eden" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight's Master</a>.<br /><br />Note to author/publisher – Given the book had a mini mystery/suspense element regarding the nature of Colin’s beast, it would have been a good idea not to identify it on the back cover blurb!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10449359771216389842" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8193328325104210430">Hot, paranormal romance, review to come. Loving Cynthia Eden.<br/><br/><br/>Review!<br/>This one had a real romantic suspense crossed with paranormal feel.<br/>We have a murderer that the people in the "know" know is a shifter. However the rest of the world is unaware of the existence of these creatures. And by creatures I don't mean just your standard vampires, shifters, demons. In this world we have every sort of creature you could ever imagine. Djinn's, charmers, witches and warlocks just to name a few. <br/>We have Emily</span>
  <span id="freeText8193328325104210430" style="display:none">Hot, paranormal romance, review to come. Loving Cynthia Eden.<br /><br /><br />Review!<br />This one had a real romantic suspense crossed with paranormal feel.<br />We have a murderer that the people in the "know" know is a shifter. However the rest of the world is unaware of the existence of these creatures. And by creatures I don't mean just your standard vampires, shifters, demons. In this world we have every sort of creature you could ever imagine. Djinn's, charmers, witches and warlocks just to name a few. <br />We have Emily Drake our heroine who can tell who is an "other" just by being near them.... and also has the special ability of being able to read there minds. She is called the monster doctor and spends her days treating vampires with a blood phobia or Charmers with problems with there animals. She gets dragged into a murder investigation to weedle out the killer by using her abilities. <br />Colin Gyth the lead investigator, is not just your average policeman. He is a shifter, but he is leading a secret life, not wanting anyone to know what he is. He seeks out Emily to make her keep his secret but sparks fly and when they are forced to work with one another their relationship develops. <br /><br />This was an amazingly entertaining read. I was sucked in, by the world and the characters. The mystery kept me guessing until the very end. Colin was a super hot shifter hero and I loved listening to him figure out his feelings in regards to Emily. Emily was a great heroine, no simpering miss, she had a tough background, she was a survivor and I respected everything about her. <br />Cythia Edens writing is easy to follow and the storyline although fast paced, is never rushed. The only think I was interested in finding out and didn't was the connection between McNeal and Emily.... the secret history intrigued me. <br />Great start to a series and I will be reading on.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76550839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer680101482185821823">Emily is a human (or <i>is</i> she??) psychic psychologist, affectionately known as the Monster Doctor. Colin is a sexy shifter cop. (But what kind of shifter is he? Were's are the most dangerous. And volatile. And they <i>mate for life</i>. And must be avoided at all cost because they are so dangerous. Has it been mentioned that they are dangerous? Boy, oh boy I hope the cop is anything but a were!)<br/><br/>Let's see, Emily hasn't been in a relationship for a while, dresses sensibly, and is sex-ay. Sound familiar? Se</span>
  <span id="freeText680101482185821823" style="display:none">Emily is a human (or <i>is</i> she??) psychic psychologist, affectionately known as the Monster Doctor. Colin is a sexy shifter cop. (But what kind of shifter is he? Were's are the most dangerous. And volatile. And they <i>mate for life</i>. And must be avoided at all cost because they are so dangerous. Has it been mentioned that they are dangerous? Boy, oh boy I hope the cop is anything but a were!)<br><br>Let's see, Emily hasn't been in a relationship for a while, dresses sensibly, and is sex-ay. Sound familiar? Secret-shifter cop Colin can't control his over-hyped hormones from the moment he meets Emily and proceeds to tell her over and over how much he wants her. Although Emily frequently tells him no, on the inside she laments, <i>"How could she hunger so much for someone that she feared?"</i><br><br>Who remembers the episode "Life on the Fast Lane" from season one of The Simpsons? In it, Marge almost has a romance with Jacques, her smarmy bowling instructor. At one point Jacques says to Marge, "Your mouth says no, but your heart, and your loins, say YES!" <br><br><span>[image error]</span><i>Why am I always reminded of this scene when reading so many bad romances???</i><br><br><br>But, this review is about <i>Hotter After Midnight</i>, not The Simpsons. So, Emily continues to resist Colin's charms, which pretty much consist of him frequently giving her smoldering stares and eloquently stating, "You want me." Poor Emily is powerless to resist such manly candor. <i>"He'd told her that he was coming over to talk about the Other, not for a date. But she'd still wasted all that time on the meal. Wasted time showering and dressing. She'd even left her hair down, not that Colin had seemed to notice."</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380328718i/691735._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>Oh man, don't you just hate it when you go through all the trouble of getting showered and dressed and your company doesn't even appreciate it??</i> <br><br>Colin, however could most definitely notice, as is evidenced by this observation, <i>"...he could smell the sweet scent of her woman's cream in the air."</i> Ew! Just, ew.<br><br>Before long, <i>"His cock sprang forward, lunging for her eager hands. He hadn't bothered with underwear. Never did."</i> <br>Oh yeah, going commando. Like a boss. <br><br>Despite all of the cheese, <i>Hotter After Midnight</i> started out fairly promising. It featured a murder mystery and an interesting paranormal world. However, the more the writing focused on Emily and Colin hooking up, the less the writing focused on continuing to make the plot believable or interesting. As for Emily and Colin themselves, I found neither one likable or fresh. We have read Emily's character so many times in so many urban fantasy and paranormal romance novels. Colin is that rogue cop who does it his own way and just doesn't give a damn about the rules. Yawn.<br><br>This really wasn’t bad, for what it is. But considering the plethora of awesome books that are still waiting to be read, this is a series which I will not be continuing. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="680101482185821823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14773409022030622929">It's hard for me to definitively describe this book as erotica vs. romance. I will say that I enjoyed reading this book. <br/><br/>Emily is the Monster Doctor, a shrink for the monsters. When we first meet Emily, she is trying to help a newly turned vamp who is disgusted by the thought of drinking blood! Emily herself is human, but has always had the ability to recognize the "Other". When Emily is called in to profile a serial killer, it becomes clear that the killer is an "Other". If that wasn't bad enou</span>
  <span id="freeText14773409022030622929" style="display:none">It's hard for me to definitively describe this book as erotica vs. romance. I will say that I enjoyed reading this book. <br /><br />Emily is the Monster Doctor, a shrink for the monsters. When we first meet Emily, she is trying to help a newly turned vamp who is disgusted by the thought of drinking blood! Emily herself is human, but has always had the ability to recognize the "Other". When Emily is called in to profile a serial killer, it becomes clear that the killer is an "Other". If that wasn't bad enough, she has to work with Colin, a cop who is a shifter of some sort, but doesn't want anyone to know and isn't thrilled that Emily can 'out' him. These two are fighting a powerful attraction for each other from the beginning. I enjoyed the storyline, and seeing these two learn about each other and how to work together.<br /><br />I'd definately read this author again.<br /><br />***Breaking news: This author has two upcoming releases...she's in the anthology "Everlasting Bad Boys" with Shelly Laurenston and Noelle Mack due out in August 08. Also "Midnight Sins" with more about the 'Other' due out in November of 08! Thanks to Kym for the tip on "Midnight Sins".</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5015892282270196019"><b>*1,5 stars*</b><br/><br/>It took me a week to read this book. Partly because of lack of reading time but also because when I finally could find time to read, I couldn't be bothered to do it. Here's why:<br/>1/ The plot was lame. <br/>2/ There was no characters development whatsoever.<br/>3/ As a result, I couldn't connect with the heroes.<br/>4/ The end was botched. But as the plot was lame to begin with, I suppose that this was to be expected. <br/><br/>That being said, I think this author has good books, I just picked poorly. <br/><br/><br/></span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/627337-tina?shelf=romance-paranormal">romance-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/627337-tina?shelf=z2010-reads">z2010-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/627337-tina?shelf=sff-urban-fantasy">sff-urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79814470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2316061488454252394"><i>"Never trust anything normal. Cuz it's the normal stuff you've got to fear. Monsters, demons, witches...we're all more afraid of that normal world than you can ever imagine."</i><br/><br/>Dr. Emily Drake is psychiatrist to the paranormal. She listens to the woes of vampires who have blood phobias and succubi who just want to find true love. In a world where shifters, vampires, witches and demons all live a secret life hidden from the awareness of most humans, Emily is different. She is a human that can see pa</span>
  <span id="freeText2316061488454252394" style="display:none"><i>"Never trust anything normal. Cuz it's the normal stuff you've got to fear. Monsters, demons, witches...we're all more afraid of that normal world than you can ever imagine."</i><br /><br />Dr. Emily Drake is psychiatrist to the paranormal. She listens to the woes of vampires who have blood phobias and succubi who just want to find true love. In a world where shifters, vampires, witches and demons all live a secret life hidden from the awareness of most humans, Emily is different. She is a human that can see paranormals. Not only see them, she knows what kind they are and how powerful they are.<br /><br />Colin Gyth is a cop. And a shifter. he wonders why his captain has requested the presence of a psychiatrist to the scene of a grisly murder. But Colin soon realizes with shock what Emily is. His own identity as a shifter is a highly guarded secret. His last partner, when he found out what Colin was, attempted to kill him. So Colin keeps his paranormal identity under wraps.<br /><br />But as soon as Emily sees him she knows what he is. The two are thrown together to find the killer -- a paranormal creature who is not done killing.<br /><br />I got this book as a free kindle download. I had not read this author before and only got it to have "just in case." I wasn't even particularly interested in reading a paranormal either, but the first few chapters really caught my eye. And then i really got immersed in the story.<br /><br />First, I like that the author has created a world with some pretty evident rules. In this case the paranormal community is not out in the open, there are a lot of different paranormal "races". Like only recognizes like. Paranormals know another paranormal when they see one, but they may not know exactly what type another one is. And Emily can see them all and can place their power level from a range of one to ten.<br /><br />Second, I like that the book was a nice hybrid of styles. It was a romance, but it was also a mystery/police procedural. And the love scenes had a nice erotica flavor to them. <br /><br />And third, I really liked the supporting cast. Breakout characters include Niol, the very powerful demon who runs the 'Other' bar known as Paradise Found. this is a series so I hope we get to see much more of Niol. Colin's partner, Brooks, was also intriguing. And I couldn't help but feel bad for the guy. He was kept out of the loop of the investigation because Colin was so freaked about his last partner. I also liked the captain, Danny and love the fact that he and the gorgeous ME Smith had a little vibe going.<br /><br />When I finished the book, i found that I enjoyed it so much that I really wanted to go and get the second one. So i downloaded it right then. Curse you Kindle! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2316061488454252394" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer584282663" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12514857561532629343">Review posted on <a href='http://www.gotfiction.com/hotter-after-midnight-by-cynthia-eden/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Got Fiction?</a><br/>Emily Drake can see things normal humans can’t. She knows all about the things that go bump in the night. And because she can see them, she knows more than most humans do. They call her the Monster Doc, but she’s a psychiatrist for the Others.<br/><br/>Colin Gyth is a cop, and he’s a good one. But he’s also more. He’s a shifter. When his captain sends him to Emily’s office to have her consult on a case, he’s doesn’t know why they need her, but after one look into her eyes, he’</span>
  <span id="freeText12514857561532629343" style="display:none">Review posted on <a href="http://www.gotfiction.com/hotter-after-midnight-by-cynthia-eden/" rel="nofollow noopener">Got Fiction?</a><br />Emily Drake can see things normal humans can’t. She knows all about the things that go bump in the night. And because she can see them, she knows more than most humans do. They call her the Monster Doc, but she’s a psychiatrist for the Others.<br /><br />Colin Gyth is a cop, and he’s a good one. But he’s also more. He’s a shifter. When his captain sends him to Emily’s office to have her consult on a case, he’s doesn’t know why they need her, but after one look into her eyes, he’s lost for her.<br /><br />There’s a killer out there, and he isn’t human. He’s taunting them and hiding from them, but Colin doesn’t know what he’s dealing with. For being a shifter, he knows surprisingly little about the Other. Emily gives him a crash course on Others 101, but there’s a lot more going on than either of them can guess.<br /><br />I liked the fact that the big bad alpha hero didn’t know anything about his world. He didn’t know what to do with his feelings toward Emily, and that he was protective of her while also recognizing that the fragile human was pretty scrappy. She wasn’t going down without a fight.<br /><br />The killer was a surprise, and even though I’ve read this before I’d totally forgotten who it was. I also loved the fact that a lot of this story takes place in the police station. I mean, not literally, but more in the sense that we see how the police would handle Other crimes, and how human cops who don’t know about them are kept in the dark. It’s interesting and I think I’ll reread the whole series.<br /><br />This book is sexy, intense, and kept me guessing. If you love Paranormal Romance, you’ll love this. If you love Romantic Suspense, you’ll love this. Cynthia Eden blends the paranormal aspect with the thriller aspect so well, you’ll feel like you’re right there in her world.<br /><br />***I bought this book but it’s also available on Kindle Unlimited</span>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1283263443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13091704143990358278">Hotter After Midnight has a little bit of everything. It has mystery, gore, sexy scenes, a romance between a shifter and a human and some great suspense moments. Doctor Emily Drake has been dubbed the Monster Doctor since she helps the supernatural deal with issues that she has a special ability to gain insight to. She is going about her business as usual when she is called to help on a grizzly murder case which puts her right into the cross-hairs of a killer. I enjoyed this story which has many</span>
  <span id="freeText13091704143990358278" style="display:none">Hotter After Midnight has a little bit of everything. It has mystery, gore, sexy scenes, a romance between a shifter and a human and some great suspense moments. Doctor Emily Drake has been dubbed the Monster Doctor since she helps the supernatural deal with issues that she has a special ability to gain insight to. She is going about her business as usual when she is called to help on a grizzly murder case which puts her right into the cross-hairs of a killer. I enjoyed this story which has many signature moments from Eden. It is fast paced and the romance never takes over the plot too much. I loved Emily and Colin and was excited to see them find clues and catch a killer. I definitely recommend to Eden fans and fans of paranormal romance suspense! </span>

<div id="review_1225594798" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1225594798" />
    <a title="Marianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16417346-marianne"><img alt="Marianne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528189144p2/16417346.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1225594798?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marianne" href="/user/show/16417346-marianne">Marianne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16417346-marianne?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16417346-marianne?shelf=shapeshifters-weres-dragons-etc">shapeshifters-weres-dragons-etc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16417346-marianne?shelf=demons-devils-gargoyles">demons-devils-gargoyles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16417346-marianne?shelf=smuttylicious">smuttylicious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16417346-marianne?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16417346-marianne?shelf=thriller-and-or-detective-work">thriller-and-or-detective-work</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1225594798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13815432501059200546">Just finished reading the Midnight trilogy by Cynthia Eden and I must say I really enjoyed the books about the Others & the humans that grow to love them. Each story can be read individually, but you'll enjoy the books more if you read them all, in order. (Because while each book is a standalone, with a separate love story, there is also a fourth love story that takes place over the course of all three books.)<br/><br/>In the first book we meet Dr. Emily Drake. Known as the Monster Doctor, she's not your </span>
  <span id="freeText13815432501059200546" style="display:none">Just finished reading the Midnight trilogy by Cynthia Eden and I must say I really enjoyed the books about the Others &amp; the humans that grow to love them. Each story can be read individually, but you'll enjoy the books more if you read them all, in order. (Because while each book is a standalone, with a separate love story, there is also a fourth love story that takes place over the course of all three books.)<br /><br />In the first book we meet Dr. Emily Drake. Known as the Monster Doctor, she's not your average shrink, Her patients consist of vampires, shifters, charmers, and demons. Emily has the ability to sense the emotions of non-humans, and she uses her talent to help them navigate the trials and tribulations of being Other in a society that are either cluless of their existence - or view them as as highly dangerous.<br /><br />Her only rule: Never trust a shifter, especially the wolves, who can be both unstable and psychotic.<br /><br />Unfortunately, Colin Gyth is just that, a shifter... and a detective. Having been burned before, he goes through great pains to hide who he is from those around him. As a cop, he knows how dangerous life is even without admitting to others the beast that he carries inside him. When victims start turning up with their throats ripped out and animal hairs on their bodies, Colin is determined to get to the bottom of things before anyone else turns up dead. And the Monster Doctor is just what he needs: Not only as a profiler, getting to hang out with the beautiful, but wary, green-eyed empath is just a perk that comes with the job. Even if his inner beast is starting to act awfully obsessive when it comes to the little human.<br /><br />I relly enjoyed the first book in this series that is a mix of UP,PNR,suspense and thriller. The supporting cast was what made this book so enjoyable. Emily's client base is really something: A succubus who wants a meaningful relationship, not just casual sex; a charmer who is despairing because her snake companion is giving her the silent treatment; and a vampire with a severe case of blood phobia. I call that highly entertaining &amp; original! Then there's Todd Brooke, Colin's tought - but clueless partner - and the powerfully dangerous demon Niol who refuses to hide what he is... <br /><br />Lucky for me, two of my favorite characters get their own books as well, because Cara, the dysfunctional succubus and the dangerous level 10 demon Niol really piqued my interest in this first installment - and their books didn't disappoint either:-)<br /><br />4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13815432501059200546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_212366295" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/212366295" />
    <a title="MsRomanticReads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596362-msromanticreads"><img alt="MsRomanticReads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1381385780p2/4596362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/212366295?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MsRomanticReads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MsRomanticReads" href="/user/show/4596362-msromanticreads">MsRomanticReads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596362-msromanticreads?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596362-msromanticreads?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596362-msromanticreads?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596362-msromanticreads?shelf=shifters">shifters</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer212366295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4604523752525698524"><br/><br/>As far as I'm concerned, this book is hot before, during and after midnight. I really liked this story, the first of the <i>Midnight Trilogy</i>. Emily Drake has been able to see the <i>Other</i> (as in all mythical creatures) ever since she was a child. Now she's a shrink to the things that are the cause of what goes bump in the night. That's actually a rather cute idea. When savagely mutilated body of a demon turns up, an old friend and Captain of the Atlanta PD calls her in for her help. <br/><br/>Detective Colin Gy</span>
  <span id="freeText4604523752525698524" style="display:none"><br /><br />As far as I'm concerned, this book is hot before, during and after midnight. I really liked this story, the first of the <i>Midnight Trilogy</i>. Emily Drake has been able to see the <i>Other</i> (as in all mythical creatures) ever since she was a child. Now she's a shrink to the things that are the cause of what goes bump in the night. That's actually a rather cute idea. When savagely mutilated body of a demon turns up, an old friend and Captain of the Atlanta PD calls her in for her help. <br /><br />Detective Colin Gyth is instantly weary of the gorgeous psychic doctor who seems to know <i>what</i> he is. She tempts him like no other woman ever has and he knows he's in trouble when his protective instincts flare up where she's concerned. Because, shifters are very protective of only their mates, aren't they? <br /><br />The schmexy times outweighed the suspense in this book. Personally, I don't find that a bad thing because I loved the chemistry between Emily and Colin and watching them try to figure out where they were headed was very cute. It was one of those light, feel-good reads with a touch of danger. Just what I needed to unwind after a horrible day. Thank you Ms Eden for making my blood hammer, lol. Now, may I please have a Colin too? </span>
  <a data-text-id="4604523752525698524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6487314512309882150">This review was posted at <a href='http://underthecoversbookblog.blogspot.com/2011/08/review-hotter-after-midnight-by-cynthia.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Under The Covers</a><br/><br/>This book was a recommendation from November's Pick It For Me Challenge. I ended up reading a different book for the challenge, but this one seemed like a good story and I couldn't be happier right now that I chose to read it.<br/><br/>There was hot, explosive and raw chemistry between the hero & heroine.   <span id="freeText6487314512309882150" style="display:none">This review was posted at <a href="http://underthecoversbookblog.blogspot.com/2011/08/review-hotter-after-midnight-by-cynthia.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Under The Covers</a><br /><br />This book was a recommendation from November's Pick It For Me Challenge. I ended up reading a different book for the challenge, but this one seemed like a good story and I couldn't be happier right now that I chose to read it.<br /><br />There was hot, explosive and raw chemistry between the hero &amp; heroine. I liked Emily's character (shrink for the Others, Monster Doctor, LOL) and the fact that, while being human, she can sense/feel SBs (Supernatural Beings). Colin also did a very good representation of a shifter, of course I had figured out what type he was, and don't really know why it was a big secret!<br /><br />I had suspicions about a couple of different people being the killer throughout the book, the actual killer among them a couple of times but I ended up dismissing him.<br /><br />I can't wait to read more about this series since we also met some pretty interesting characters (McNeal) that I wouldn't mind reading more about.</span>

<div id="review_239059591" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="The BookChick " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6190526-the-bookchick"><img alt="The BookChick " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546023730p2/6190526.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/239059591?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The BookChick " class="user" itemprop="url" name="The BookChick " href="/user/show/6190526-the-bookchick">The BookChick </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6190526-the-bookchick?shelf=4-star-read">4-star-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer239059591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8562583862909775524">I loved this story. Colin and Emily were likeable characters that were dynamic and interesting.<br/><br/>Emily Drake was a psychic empath who was a psychologist to the <i>Other</i>, supernatural beings including demons, shifters, charmers, etc. Brought in on a case by our hero, Colin Gyth, a detective for the Alanta PD and a shifter, Emily's life takes on a roller coaster pace. She is used as a profiler for a highly public murder where the suspect butchered his victim, thus being dubbed the Night Butcher.<br/><br/>Through</span>
  <span id="freeText8562583862909775524" style="display:none">I loved this story. Colin and Emily were likeable characters that were dynamic and interesting.<br /><br />Emily Drake was a psychic empath who was a psychologist to the <i>Other</i>, supernatural beings including demons, shifters, charmers, etc. Brought in on a case by our hero, Colin Gyth, a detective for the Alanta PD and a shifter, Emily's life takes on a roller coaster pace. She is used as a profiler for a highly public murder where the suspect butchered his victim, thus being dubbed the Night Butcher.<br /><br />Through a series of interesting twists, Colin and Emily work together using her abilities and his knowledge as a detective and shifter, to catch the butcher before he strikes again. <br /><br />It was a well written story and I appreciated the unexpected Night Butcher villain. My only problem with the story is that Eden didn't really flesh out why the butcher was the way he was. She glossed over an explanation that I felt should/could have been more than two or three sentences. Hence the 4 stars instead of 5.<br /><br />But overall, this was a very enjoyable read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8562583862909775524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_140114955" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140114955" />
    <a title="Tracy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4250430-tracy"><img alt="Tracy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1283724040p2/4250430.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140114955?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tracy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tracy" href="/user/show/4250430-tracy">Tracy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6706210-hotter-after-midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4250430-tracy?shelf=paranormal-romantic-suspense">paranormal-romantic-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140114955" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10816718906142887677">This is my first foray into books by Cynthia Eden and I'm happy to note that it was a very pleasant trip. Well...perhaps pleasant isn't quite the right word...<br/><br/>Dr. Emily Drake is a very special psychologist. She sees demons. And vampires. And shifters. And a legion of Other supernatural beings that inhabit the world alongside us. She's one of the few full humans who know of the existence of Others but she's also got a bit of a leg up - she's the only one she's met who can sense them like she can.</span>
  <span id="freeText10816718906142887677" style="display:none">This is my first foray into books by Cynthia Eden and I'm happy to note that it was a very pleasant trip. Well...perhaps pleasant isn't quite the right word...<br /><br />Dr. Emily Drake is a very special psychologist. She sees demons. And vampires. And shifters. And a legion of Other supernatural beings that inhabit the world alongside us. She's one of the few full humans who know of the existence of Others but she's also got a bit of a leg up - she's the only one she's met who can sense them like she can. Known as the Monster Doctor among Others, she uses her empathic abilities to aid those creatures who go bump in the night, because in Dr. Drake's world, just because they bump doesn't mean they don't have issues. The Others are like us in one very important way - some are good to varying degrees, and some...well, some aren't. The problem is that when an Other is evil, the level of carnage can multiply exponentially. When the ravaged body of a human is discovered - one who definitely went the way of fangs and claws - who else but the Monster Doctor could ever hope to help the police in general, and one very sexy shifter, Detective Colin Gyth in particular, profile and stop this psychopathic Other from painting the city red.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2754526.Hotter_After_Midnight__Midnight___1_" title="Hotter After Midnight (Midnight, #1) by Cynthia Eden" rel="nofollow noopener">Hotter After Midnight</a>, was a nice surprise. Eden has created a believable world full of interesting paranormal characters and paired it with a decent romantic suspense plot. The blend works well together and as I'm a huge fan of both paranormal romance and romantic suspense, this juxtaposition impressed me.<br /><br />The lead characters, Emily and Colin, were sizzling hot together, and I think the development of their relationship was one of the more satisfying I've read recently because of the level of communication between them. It was nice to read a couple that could admit potentially embarrassing things about themselves, and having a female lead that was both unashamedly sexual and unapologetically strong-willed tempered with some professed insecurities and a realistic awareness of self was not only refreshing, but much appreciated.<br /><br />The plot was strong and it moved quickly, increasing threat going hand in hand with the burgeoning relationship between Emily and Colin. There was a nice balance there. There could have been a bit more depth given to their backstory and character development, and I wasn't totally thrilled with the conclusion of the mystery, as I think it became less about solving the crimes and more about the thing responsible tipping its hand (my personal preferences lie with the former), but I wasn't so turned off that it ruined anything for me. The sex scenes were smoking hot and deliciously graphic, though once that yummy wall was breached the sexual relationship took up a bit too much of the story. I'm not complaining about that, per se, but I wonder if there'd been a bit less of it if my other slight concerns would have been more fully addressed. There were a few unanswered questions, secondary and ancillary characters that could've been fleshed out more, and a couple of things I would have enjoyed more had they been given more time to develop, but for what was here, I am a very satisfied reader and intend to continue on with the trilogy and more of Eden's books. Great read.<br /><br />~*~*~*~<br />Reviewed for <a href="http://one-good-book.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">One Good Book Deserves Another</a>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10816718906142887677" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2855030-gokce-muslin-myst?shelf=series-1st-book">series-1st-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2855030-gokce-muslin-myst?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101980795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4285702095848846121">This wasn't a bad book but it could've been better. The pace was alright, the mystery ok enough to keep you reading if not a bit predictable. The characters, however, were a different and more complex story. Emily Drake, a supernatural creature -<i>Other</i>, as they are referred in the book- psychologist helps out the police in a murder investigation with abnormal circumstances. She gets called in by a, what I can only call, good old friend, the Captain Danny McNeal to aid detective Colin Gyth in this</span>
  <span id="freeText4285702095848846121" style="display:none">This wasn't a bad book but it could've been better. The pace was alright, the mystery ok enough to keep you reading if not a bit predictable. The characters, however, were a different and more complex story. Emily Drake, a supernatural creature -<i>Other</i>, as they are referred in the book- psychologist helps out the police in a murder investigation with abnormal circumstances. She gets called in by a, what I can only call, good old friend, the Captain Danny McNeal to aid detective Colin Gyth in this murder which is without a doubt a supernatural attack. Throughout the book we're also introduced to Todd Brooks, who is partner to Colin Gyth and the character that got my interest the most, and ME Smith who seemed like had a history with McNeal and several other supernatural creatures, the most important being Niol, the dangerous demon who owns a club for the "Others".<br /><br />Emily Drake had a very very bad start to the book if you ask me and she was too close to be included to my "gal that annoyed the hell out of me" bookshelf, still don't know what saved her but whatever. She was borderline annoying at times. She's a psychologist for the Other, and yet this one time a poor vampire who has trouble drinking blood comes to her and even though she describes his problem as a very serious and deadly one she still manages to call him a drama queen. What? Have some compassion for your patients doc. Which brings me to my other annoying point. What was up with Colin calling Emily "Doc" all the freaking time? It was all "Doc this", "Doc that", "This and that, Doc"!! I got tired after a while and refused to read the word.<br /><br />Colin's character was lacking. I mean sure, the guy was there and all, we had his POV but somehow I felt like the writer could've made a better effort getting into the mental status of the guy. Sure, he wss a "shifter" who turned into a wolf so he should've had animal instincts but the only thing the guy thought about was sexsexsex. Have her.Mark her.Fuck her.Sexsexsex. And it didn't matter much whether there was danger around them or other people or they were discussing the case. Whatever, whenever. <br /><br />Danny McNeal, captain of the PD, I didn't get what he was all about. He knew about all the "Other" stuff and he kept referring to the supernaturals as "we" and yet we were never hinted towards him being a supernatural. All the time I read him as human who knew about all this but somehow the wording of the guy kinda screwed up that aspect.<br /><br />The only likeable characters in this book were Niol -the demon trouble- and Todd Brooks -Colin's partner, human, clueless- And the way Brooks was ignored all throughout the investigation, just because he didn't know about the nature of the crime and the "monsters who happen to be real", was not believable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4285702095848846121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_168200498" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168200498" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2701111-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311362224p2/2701111.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168200498?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/2701111-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2701111-emily?shelf=reviewed-books">reviewed-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168200498" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3873775014068505670">I love Cynthia Eden's paranormal romance novels and for me, this was the one that started it all. I love when I start reading a series at the beginning and the writing and characters only get better with time, and this is a very good example of that. While not the most polished book by this author, the bar is set very high from the getgo, the romance is spicy and sweet at the same time, and the characters are interesting and easy to root for.<br/><br/>One of the common issues that has to be resolved in a </span>
  <span id="freeText3873775014068505670" style="display:none">I love Cynthia Eden's paranormal romance novels and for me, this was the one that started it all. I love when I start reading a series at the beginning and the writing and characters only get better with time, and this is a very good example of that. While not the most polished book by this author, the bar is set very high from the getgo, the romance is spicy and sweet at the same time, and the characters are interesting and easy to root for.<br /><br />One of the common issues that has to be resolved in a paranormal romance that eventually sets up the rules that the folks in the book have to follow is whether or not the rest of the world knows that the paranormal people exist. In this case, most humans are decidedly unaware of the things that go bump in the night, and the supernatural community would like to keep it that way. So when they need help tracking a serial killer who's running perilously close to exposing all of them, it's fortuitous that one of the best psychologists in the city happens to specialize in treating Others.<br /><br />Dr. Emily is smart, both book smart and street smart, and all of her instincts that have kept her secret safe for so long tell her to leave Detective Colin alone, do not pass go, do not collect two hundred dollars. Colin isn't about to let that happen and he gets all snarly alpha on her in a big way. Emily is forced to reconsider her previous notions about shifters (which Colin is) and whether getting mixed up with one is good or bad for her long term well-being. Chemistry is a bitch, isn't it?<br /><br />The mystery of the identity of the Night Butcher isn't terribly hard to figure out once all the pieces are revealed and frankly, I didn't care- it was nice to have a good secondary story to support the romance. Sometimes it bugs me if I figure out the romance too early but this wasn't one of those times.<br /><br />This series dovetails into the one she writes now (Night Watch) and while you don't have to read one to get the other, it does enhance the experience, at least it did for me. While not as polished as some of the later books this one is still fun, and on a snowy, blustery day like today, fun is a good thing.<br /><br />Overall Grade: B+<br /><br />Check out more reviews and other good stuff at <a href="http://www.whatbookisthat.com" rel="nofollow noopener">What Book is That?</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3873775014068505670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3282287532631770593">Very good read - a paranormal page turner with an action plot. Romantic suspense/urban fantasy with a serial murderer plot and there are some unexpected twists before the murderer is finally revealed. The heroine Dr. Emily Drake, the so-called Monster Doctor, is drawn into a serial murder case - first to identify the paranormal elements of the case and then as the profiler on the murderer. The hero is Colin, a cop who tries fiercely to deny his werewolf nature and is appalled to find that Emily </span>
  <span id="freeText3282287532631770593" style="display:none">Very good read - a paranormal page turner with an action plot. Romantic suspense/urban fantasy with a serial murderer plot and there are some unexpected twists before the murderer is finally revealed. The heroine Dr. Emily Drake, the so-called Monster Doctor, is drawn into a serial murder case - first to identify the paranormal elements of the case and then as the profiler on the murderer. The hero is Colin, a cop who tries fiercely to deny his werewolf nature and is appalled to find that Emily can easily 'see' that he is a shifter of some sort is assigned to the case. And his wild attraction to her makes it difficult to do his job... The situation is further complicated by his human partner who needs to be kept in the dark about the paranormal elements of the case.<br /><br />I liked the humor - you've got to admit that a vampire who is afraid of blood has a REAL problem - and I liked the way the relationship unfolded between the hero/heroine. At the start she fears werewolves and he fears his own nature and exposure. Through the story they find commonality to build on. They are both outsiders - she by virtue of her powers to see and read the Others - he by growing up totally outside the community of the Others. She grows to trust him and he grows to trust her...<br /><br />I liked it well enough to order the next two books from Amazon...<br /><br />Midnight<br />Hotter After Midnight (2008) This is scheduled for re-release at the end of this year<br />Midnight Sins (2008)<br />Midnight's Master (2009)</span>

  <span id="freeText8700093522307672078" style="display:none">Emily Drake has seen monsters all her life. Shifters, Demons, Vampires and lots of other creatures that go bump in the night. She’s a shrink with a thriving clientele of Other creatures Vamps that can’t drink blood, shifter’s that can’t shift even a succubus that wants to be thought of as more than a sex symbol. Emily is also has strong empathic talents which she often uses to help her patients.<br /><br />Colin Gyth is the lead detective in a brutal homicide when his boss tells him to get Emily to take a look at the crime scene he wonders why. When he discovers that Emily has the ability to see his kind and read minds he’s less than thrilled he is worried his secrets may be exposed.<br /><br />Emily and Colin team up to catch a serial killer who is less than human. A killer that has no intention of giving up his killing rage and human are his prey. When the killer’s focus shifts to Emily Colin will do whatever it takes to keep her safe.<br /><br />Ms Eden does not disappoint Hotter than Midnight will keep you up after midnight turning those pages. Warning this book is so hard to put down. Paranormal readers will love how Ms Eden has taken a great variety of paranormal favorites added an amazing plot and a hotter than hot romance.<br />Definitely a keeper and a recommended read.</span>

<div id="review_137057837" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137057837" />
    <a title="Emanuela ~plastic duck~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4268461-emanuela-plastic-duck"><img alt="Emanuela ~plastic duck~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472332781p2/4268461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137057837?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emanuela ~plastic duck~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emanuela ~plastic duck~" href="/user/show/4268461-emanuela-plastic-duck">Emanuela ~plastic duck~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4268461-emanuela-plastic-duck?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137057837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6135513622165791704">2.5 stars.<br/><br/>I don't know what rubbed me wrong in this book. It has all the elements I usually like in romance: an interesting setting with an original interaction between humans and supernatural beings; an Alpha hero in law-enforcement; a smart heroine; no purple prose; a bit of mystery. Still I never found myself really immersed in the story, my mind was hovering and what I usually overlook when I am engrossed in a story slowly became annoying.<br/><br/>I think I didn't like the initial interaction between</span>
  <span id="freeText6135513622165791704" style="display:none">2.5 stars.<br /><br />I don't know what rubbed me wrong in this book. It has all the elements I usually like in romance: an interesting setting with an original interaction between humans and supernatural beings; an Alpha hero in law-enforcement; a smart heroine; no purple prose; a bit of mystery. Still I never found myself really immersed in the story, my mind was hovering and what I usually overlook when I am engrossed in a story slowly became annoying.<br /><br />I think I didn't like the initial interaction between hero and heroine. I like really Alpha heroes and heroines who decides to be overcome by them without trying to project a holier-than-thou attitude, but I wasn't able to believe the words spoken by the main couple. The dialogue seemed stilted, the writing didn't flow. It's probably a problem of style, of writing rhythm that didn't sit well with my tastes. I also think that Colin's past could have been explored further to make his character more rounded and less cave-man. There was probably some humor in certain situations, but it got lost on me.<br /><br />It's a pity because I think the action part was very well done and the concept of the story was well thought and original. I'll read the next book because I always take a second chance with a new (for me) author.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6135513622165791704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xRZ6B14gE9fT6cbKLDQ3DVv/fjD5/OVdZergKyYPVxpeoha8d/iQQPuPvBb1UjOMxvhMmfVw7Xh1Vb0S0ev8lA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rfPH1odbTIfnmyQYei/kEiJb8VuKDJshJ2seHDYgPmQ2R6ttroPPEM/9XsSjSeCTv1zD8oaAkwQ31EMlwcSV6g==')})
  }

Since she began writing full-time in 2005, Cynthia has written over one hundred novels and novellas.<br /><br /><br />Cynthia lives along the Alabama Gulf Coast. She loves romance novels, horror movies, and chocolate. Her favorite hobbies including hiking in the mountains (searching for waterfalls) and spelunking.</span>
